## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. The relationship encodes mechanisms like density-dependent growth, carrying capacity, and potentially time-varying environmental conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, low density)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect, negative growth at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic with Holling type II removal)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic growth rate model)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying intrinsic growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Logistic with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (constant immigration term)
- Delayed feedback approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (linear time modulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (P - P²) → classic logistic-type density dependence with a single stable equilibrium at carrying capacity
- Cubic dependence on P (P² - P³ or P·(P-a)·(1-P/K)) → Allee effect with bistability and a critical population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling log(K/P) with P → Gompertz-type growth with slower approach to carrying capacity from above than below
- Product of P with a periodic function of t → seasonally forced population dynamics with time-varying environment
- Ratio P/(P+c) or P²/(P²+c) → saturating functional response (Holling type II/III) indicating predation or resource limitation
- Difference of power laws (P^a - P^b with a < b) → metabolic scaling models balancing anabolism and catabolism
- Growth rate per capita (dP_dt/P) being linear in P → logistic model; nonlinear in P → generalized density dependence
- Exponential decay multiplied by P (e.g., P*exp(-c*t)) → population with deteriorating environmental conditions over time

$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

This is a function of P only (no t dependence). Let me note that the GT has the form:
$$\alpha P + \beta P^2 + \gamma P^2/(δP + 1)$$

where α = 0.9198, β = -0.01095, γ = 0.9198, δ = 7.531.

Now I need to check candidates that can match this structure. The key feature is the rational term $P^2/(δP + 1)$.

**Candidate 16**: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + c_2 P^2 + c_3 P^2 + c_4 P + c_5 P}{P + c_1}$

This simplifies to: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P}{P + c_1}$

Performing polynomial division: $c_0 P^3/(P+c_1) = c_0 P^2 - c_0 c_1 P + c_0 c_1^2 - c_0 c_1^3/(P+c_1)$

This gives terms with $1/(P+c_1)$ which the GT doesn't have (GT has $P^2/(δP+1)$). But let me reconsider.

The GT can be rewritten as: $\beta P^2 + \alpha P + \gamma P^2/(δP + 1)$

Combining over common denominator $(δP+1)$: $\frac{\beta P^2(δP+1) + \alpha P(δP+1) + \gamma P^2}{δP+1} = \frac{βδP^3 + (β+αδ+γ)P^2 + αP}{δP+1}$

This is $\frac{AP^3 + BP^2 + CP}{δP + 1}$. Dividing numerator and denominator by δ: $\frac{A'P^3 + B'P^2 + C'P}{P + 1/δ}$

**Candidate 16**: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P}{P + c_1}$

- $c_0 = βδ/δ = β = -0.01095$ (wait, let me be more careful)

GT numerator over $(δP+1)$: $βδP^3 + (β + αδ + γ)P^2 + αP$

Over $(P + 1/δ)$: multiply num and denom by $1/δ$:
$\frac{βP^3 + (β/δ + α + γ/δ)P^2 + (α/δ)P}{P + 1/δ}$

So: $c_0 = β = -0.01095$, $c_1 = 1/7.531 = 0.1328$, $c_2 + c_3 = β/δ + α + γ/δ$, $c_4 + c_5 = α/δ = 0.9198/7.531 = 0.1221$
